<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Titan-Earth-PolarClouds-20141024.jpg" title="Polar clouds, made of methane, on Titan (left) compared with polar clouds on Earth (right)."><img alt="" data-file-height="752" data-file-width="2000" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Titan-Earth-PolarClouds-20141024.jpg/600px-Titan-Earth-PolarClouds-20141024.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Titan-Earth-PolarClouds-20141024.jpg/900px-Titan-Earth-PolarClouds-20141024.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Titan-Earth-PolarClouds-20141024.jpg/1200px-Titan-Earth-PolarClouds-20141024.jpg 2x" width="600"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Titan-Earth-PolarClouds-20141024.jpg" title="File:Titan-Earth-PolarClouds-20141024.jpg"> </a></div>Polar clouds, made of methane, on Titan (left) compared with <a href="/wiki/Polar_stratospheric_cloud" title="Polar stratospheric cloud">polar clouds</a> on <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> (right).</div>
</div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> – the atmosphere contains 2.3% methane<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ariel_(moon)" title="Ariel (moon)">Ariel</a> – methane is believed to be a constituent of Ariel's surface ice</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miranda_(moon)" title="Miranda (moon)">Miranda</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oberon_(moon)" title="Oberon (moon)">Oberon</a> – about 20% of Oberon's surface ice is composed of methane-related carbon/nitrogen compounds</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Titania_(moon)" title="Titania (moon)">Titania</a> – about 20% of Titania's surface ice is composed of methane-related organic compounds<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Umbriel_(moon)" title="Umbriel (moon)">Umbriel</a> – methane is a constituent of Umbriel's surface ice</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a> – the atmosphere contains 1.5 ± 0.5% methane<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Triton_(moon)" title="Triton (moon)">Triton</a> – Triton has a tenuous nitrogen atmosphere with small amounts of methane near the surface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nature2_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-nature2-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grand_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-grand-118">[118]</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a> – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spectroscopic" title="Spectroscopic">spectroscopic</a> analysis of Pluto's surface reveals it to contain traces of methane<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Solstation_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Solstation-120">[120]</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Charon_(moon)" title="Charon (moon)">Charon</a> – methane is believed present on Charon, but it is not completely confirmed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eris_(dwarf_planet)" title="Eris (dwarf planet)">Eris</a> – infrared light from the object revealed the presence of methane ice<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Halley%27s_Comet" title="Halley's Comet">Halley's Comet</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Comet_Hyakutake" title="Comet Hyakutake">Comet Hyakutake</a> – terrestrial observations found <a href="/wiki/Ethane" title="Ethane">ethane</a> and methane in the comet<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-science_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-science-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" title="Extrasolar planet">Extrasolar planets</a> – methane was detected on extrasolar planet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HD_189733b" title="HD 189733b">HD 189733b</a>; this is the first detection of an organic compound on a planet outside the solar system. Its origin is unknown, since the planet's high temperature (700 °C) would normally favor the formation of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">carbon monoxide</a> instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Research indicates that <a href="/wiki/Meteoroid" title="Meteoroid">meteoroids</a> slamming against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" title="Extrasolar planet">exoplanet</a> atmospheres could add hydrocarbon gases such as methane, making the exoplanets look as though they are inhabited by life, even if they are not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Interstellar_cloud" title="Interstellar cloud">Interstellar clouds</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></li>
<li>The atmospheres of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M-type_star" title="M-type star">M-type stars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></li></ul>
